Our favorite!! Super dark, cozy, tiny restaurant with incredible delicious food.  No-nonsense service is straight to the point and not invasive or nagging but helpful.  Glorious wine list. < Text>
Had a fantastic meal there this evening. Excellent service, ambiance and the food was very good.

We had the arugula w/ pear salad and the caesar salad (with anchovies, extra on top)... both excellent with homemade dressing.

For mains we had tagliatelle and the pork chop.... both fantastic with the pasta being very fresh and the pork marinated in a brine which resulted in a very tender piece of meat.

The house wines (specifically the Tuscan) were great for our meals and the service was great. The restaurant space is small but not cramped and allows for the servers to focus on the tables they have.

Great place; look forward to coming back!<//Text>

<rate>4</rate>< Review>
This adorable little restaurant is easy to miss even though it's on a prime corner. It is a great spot to grab a bite to eat and people watch while in North Beach.
I got the cream of mushroom soup and the pork chop. The soup was amazing, but the pork chop was a little tough for my taste. The bread they serve is a focaccia bread, but the taste and texture reminded me of a donut...and anyone who has read my reviews will tell you that I love donuts! So in other words, the bread is amaze-balls!
They say they prefer cash but they do except credit cards. It's a nice spot for a date or a casual dining experience. They have wines by the bottle, but not by the glass.</Review>

<response>None< /response><username>Emily Wang< /username><gmapID>0x808580f01ee9e7f9:0x5ca46157cdfdfa13< /gmapID><Text>My friend made dinner reservations for us, but the place was basically empty when we arrived Wednesday @ 7pm.

Restaurant is small (seats around 20) and is dimly lit. Very quiet, so not ideal for a first date, but good spot to bring a date you want to get to know better.

Menu is handwritten in cursive and is hard to read, but the food makes up for it.

First, the handmade foccacia bread (free) is delicious. Soft, fluffy, and savory... we asked for seconds and our waitress obliged happily.

For appetizers, we had the arugula pear salad and the sweet potato gnocchi. Salad was light and refreshing - loved the combo of sweet pear and savory cheese. And the sweet potato gnocchi... Oh. My. Goodness. You MUST try it. Amazing. I couldn't stop telling my coworkers about it the next day, and I will definitely bring friends here if just to introduce them to it and the foccacia bread alone. 1.5x the appetizer size would probably be enough for a light dinner, since the gnocchi is fairly heavy. Next time I will definitely consider that.

For my entree, I got the penne rigate with sausage and mushrooms. Portion was relatively small, and quality was just slightly above average. Slightly undercooked pasta, but the sauce was decent.

Service was okay. Our waitress brought us the wrong appetizer at first but apologized for it.

Despite the mediocre entree, I still have to give this place 5 stars for the foccacia, sweet potato gnocchi, and quiet/romantic ambiance and decor. I will definitely bring friends here again soon.

--

Water glasses never filled until we asked. Entree (risotto) was not good - I literally didn't touch mine. Revising my review to 4 stars... < Review>
Poor quality, poor support.  Purchased a remanufactured engine for Jeep Grand Cherokee but had low oil pressure once installed.  Checked oil pressure sensor, pick up tube, filter etc.  all fine.  Called Jeep parts depot within the 90 day warranty period they said the owner was out of the country (?) so they could only sell the engines but suggested I use heavier weight oil since that cleared up a similar problem in his wife's Jeep.  When that didn't work (surprise) they blamed a faulty oil pressure sensor even though that had been tried three different times.  When finally was able to get an actual pressure reading it was truly too low.  Called Jeeppartsdepot back and they said it now outside the 90 day window so they didn't have any obligation for the defective engine.  Now, 18-months later, the head components are degrading due to insufficient oil circulation.  Three independent mechanics have looked at it and concluded the crankshaft main bearings were installed incorrectly.  The time and money I have spent to figure this out has easily outweighed my initial 'savings'.  The engine they sold me indicates either they do not know what they are doing or they don't care.  Buyer beware!<//Review>

< Review>
This is the place when people want to spend minimum money for AYCE Korean BBQ in local area. It only costs $19.99 per person to get a different kind of meat and seafood. I love to eat beef belly, rib fingers, and pork belly because they have good quality.  Also, it has mini salad bar which I love to grab tofu, fish cakes as much as I want. The service here is great, and food always cone out fast as well.  Also, beer is not expensive here for a mud size so next time I may order one as well.

It is very good place for 2 or more people to come here for BBQ because it has good environment, good quality of meat, and services.<//Review>

<Rate>4</Rate><username>Bruce Wilder</username>< review>
Went there as part of an Christmas Office party, where our group was distributed to several tables.  The place is clean, well-designed and brightly lit, upstairs in a somewhat shabby multi-use complex.  Tables typically seat 4 around a stainless grill at the center of the table, where you cook your own meat selections.

You order meats from a long menu -- including marinated beef, pork and chicken as well as unmarinated selections like steak, bacon ("pork bellies") and shrimp.  The staff will deliver up to three meat choices at a time to the table and you share.  Standard tableware are chopsticks and a single steel tong to be used in common to turn the meat.  There's a self-serve salad bar where you can also get some grillable accompaniments.

The grill surface is stainless steel and the staff will lift it off and replace it with a clean unit after your first round of meats.  There's a button on the table to summon a server when you are ready to order a second round of meats.  Theoretically, it is all you can eat, but two rounds was all we could manage.

This was my first experience with Korean BBQ and I think the newbie would want someone more experienced along for a first ride.  How satisfied you are is likely to vary with how successful you are in selecting meats and managing the cooking process and the traditional Korean condiments.  As simple as it is -- and there's nothing complicated about laying meat on the grill and turning it over when it appears to be done -- you will want some reassuring instruction from your companions.  The staff may be used to instructing newcomers -- I don't know because we had some experienced diners among us.  Service, as far as bringing meat and clearing the table, was efficient but not particular friendly or interactive -- that might not be case if you were not part of a large office party as i was.

The apparent quality of meat was very high.  I found the marinated beef especially tasty.  I am not sure I like sharing my table with a very hot grill, but that's necessary to the experience i suppose.  Other people i know said Honey Pig is as good as it gets in the Korean BBQ category.

Pricing seemed fair.  Standard gratuities are added to the bill.</review>

<Text>The atmosphere in the restaurant is perfect. Nice music and clean table wares. Service is average. BUT the star of any restaurant has to be the food which, at Honey Pig 2.0, is what I find very lacking in taste and quality. While the price tag seems pretty good for an average Korean barbecue restaurant, the quality is just not there.
First, let's start with the sides because that is what you will have to walk up and get it yourself in a buffet style which is fine. There are typical Korean sides such as kimchi, rice, mash potatoes, etc. what strikes me the most is the fried chicken which is stone cold. Kimchi tastes like it is bought from a store that comes in a plastic jar container.
Moving on to the meat which is very lacking in consistency. Brisket sometimes come with extreme amount of fat and no fat at all. Beef short ribs are very tough like rubber. Beef galbi came in a very strange condition. The beef itself is charred and seems like it has been partially cooked once before it was served.
Overall, the restaurant fails to highlight the most important thing, the food.<//Text>< Name>
steven Lai</Name>

<Text>Went during lunch time on Friday. The service was prompt and attentive. Refills were prompt, food came out quickly, the dishes were nice and clean, the side dish bar was nice and well stocked.

Best part? The pork belly, the marinated pork belly was delicious and full of flavor, the kalbi was boneless and prebbq'd lightly so it wouldn't take forever to cook on the hot plate.

<Pics>None<//Pics><Review>I don't know about you, but when it comes to restaurants, I am very picky of how the host/ hostess greet you upon arrival to their restaurant. I have to say Tony who happens to be the owner of this restaurant was an excellent greeter as well..:-)

While we were seating at our table he inquired about how we heard of his restaurant ..

We started our meal with their delicious bread basket along with olive oil and balsamic. As for our entree, we got the Halibut special as well as Spaghetti with meat sauce... I have to say the fish was moist and cooked perfectly. As for my pasta, it was a bit on the salty side and I would have liked it if it had some marinara sauce on the side or something.

We could not end our meal w/o trying one of their delicious desserts. So we got the berry tart for to go.
The tart was very delicious and it wasn't too sweet. The berries were fresh and just perfect.

So why did I deduct a star? Well our server was a bit fake... I didn't like that.<//Review>< time>

<review>We had the most fabulous Christmas Eve dinner for our family of eleven. It was elegant, gracious dining with fresh, delicious food.  We loved it so much that we're going again tonight!
We've been searching for this kind of a restaurant for a couple years and now we found it so close to home! We had read old reviews so wondered, but the new owner has it together! Everything from the service to the freshly baked bread to the fresh fish, pasta and dessert was excellent.  And it's so cozy and elegant inside - how wonderful not to have to yell across a table to be heard as is the case in so many "new cuisine" restaurants.  Here the linen clothed tables, carpeting and elegant decor make for a romantic and intimate setting complete with classical piano played by a real person not a player piano!  yay!!  I add this because I've noticed that many newer restaurants no longer have real people playing the piano, instead they have some kind of player piano that just plays by itself.
So, I highly recommend this restaurant to anyone.<//review></record>

<Date>1351721320339</Date><rating>5< /rating>< text>
Introduced some Korean and Korean-American folks to this place, and they all think it's the best Italian place they've ever been to and one of the best (if not the best) restaurant they've been to in the Glendale.  In fact, I've been here 3 times in the past week due to out of town co-workers hearing about the raves, and I'm not tired of it (and I get tired of restaurants quickly).

That said, this really is a great place.  Nice converted house atmosphere with a live piano music.  Fresh ingredients--I often get the daily special (usually one pasta and one meat/fish item).  Be sure to add a little cheese and pepper to the minestrone soup (Italian vegetable), and it's delicious.  Also, best tiramisu ever, although I like some of the other desserts, too. This place is never full - 5 stars..<//text>

< review>
This gym is solid. I only attend the Boxing classes with Vernon and Manny. Basically, Vernon focuses on technique and combos while Manny is straight conditioning and repetition. The best part of this gym is you get to know a lot of people, and I have to admit, they're a good crowd. But don't get me wrong, this is not a social gym. You will work out hard and sweat no matter what shape you're in. It's the kind of workout you can only get when working with others, because right at that moment when you are about to give up, you look around and see everyone else sweating and pushing hard, it just makes you find an inner strength that keeps you going. You will leave feeling accomplished and overall I'd say it's a great alternative to other gyms since you have access to free weight and cardio equipment, as well.</review>

<review>I've wanted to learn boxing/Kickboxing and Brazilian Jiu Jitsu for some time now. I did the whole search the web, travel to the place, talk to the people that work there and what not. My first try was Arena on Sports Arena Blvd and the guy gave me what they offered and a 30 day breakable contract. Then I told him I'm in the military and he started going off on all the Spec War guys he trains and how they asked him to rewrite their hand to hand combat book. I'm cool with that, good on you, but don't use it as a selling pitch. It just turns me off

Then I went to City Boxing and talked with them. Very kind, very professional staff. I was walked around the facility, met the trainers, shown a schedule that works with my hectic schedule and it was done. Went for training the next day and learned a ton of new things in the 3+ hours I was there. All the trainers are really helpful and will help you every step of the way; fixing form, helping you understand the movements and when they can be used. Vernon is a great boxing trainer, always willing to help you understand how to do the foot work and the strikes. Baruch is a great BJJ instructor. I have learned so much about Jiu Jitzu in my 2 days there and caught on quick.

It's a great atmosphere, professional/friendly staff, and they at least remember your name. Great place for anyone wanting to learn Jiu Mics, boxing, and Kickboxing. Really affordable prices. Paid a lump sum of 650 bucks for a year. $54 a month, that's an unbeatable price!< /review>< Pics>

This gym is solid. I only attend the Boxing classes with Vernon and Manny. Basically, Vernon focuses on technique and combos while Manny is straight conditioning and repetition. The best part of this gym is you get to know a lot of people, and I have to admit, they're a good crowd. But don't get me wrong, this is not a social gym. You will work out hard and sweat no matter what shape you're in. It's the kind of workout you can only get when working with others, because right at that moment when you are about to give up, you look around and see everyone else sweating and pushing hard, it just makes you find an inner strength that keeps you going. You will leave feeling accomplished and overall I'd say it's a great alternative to other gyms since you have access to free weight and cardio equipment, as well.< /review>

<rating>5< /rating>< Review>
I've wanted to learn boxing/Kickboxing and Brazilian Jiu Jitsu for some time now. I did the whole search the web, travel to the place, talk to the people that work there and what not. My first try was Arena on Sports Arena Blvd and the guy gave me what they offered and a 30 day breakable contract. Then I told him I'm in the military and he started going off on all the Spec War guys he trains and how they asked him to rewrite their hand to hand combat book. I'm cool with that, good on you, but don't use it as a selling pitch. It just turns me off

Then I went to City Boxing and talked with them. Very kind, very professional staff. I was walked around the facility, met the trainers, shown a schedule that works with my hectic schedule and it was done. Went for training the next day and learned a ton of new things in the 3+ hours I was there. All the trainers are really helpful and will help you every step of the way; fixing form, helping you understand the movements and when they can be used. Vernon is a great boxing trainer, always willing to help you understand how to do the foot work and the strikes. Baruch is a great BJJ instructor. I have learned so much about Jiu Jitzu in my 2 days there and caught on quick.

It's a great atmosphere, professional/friendly staff, and they at least remember your name. Great place for anyone wanting to learn Jiu Mics, boxing, and Kickboxing. Really affordable prices. Paid a lump sum of 650 bucks for a year. $54 a month, that's an unbeatable price!< /Review>

<Time>1612856979083<//Time><rating>3<//rating>< text>
Remember when Slater's first showed up? Yes, me too, but I didn't go then. Nope. All the rage...and I still didn't go. I finally went yesterday. I got the original 50/50 & it was just okay. I don't know what I expected, but for me the patty tasted more like a fatty hamburger. I didn't really taste the bacon so much. My husband claimed that it tasted more like a little bit of ham in with a beef patty. However, the brioche bun was delicious, and the egg and avocado tasty too. Tots were perfectly crisp and the bacon ketchup was more of a textural thing for me. I could tell there was something in my ketchup but again, it didn't really taste like bacon. I think I'll stick to bacon on top of my burgers. The server was absolutely sweet & she did a great job! Would I go back? Sure. I just don't know that I would order that again. I'll stick to 100% beef or chicken. The 50/50 just didn't do it for me. Meh. ü§∑</text>

Patrick Harris< /username>
<Date>1506618477389<//Date><Rating>5</Rating>< Text>
I've had Slater's on my list for several years but was never close enough to justify going there. Finally I've tried it and it lives up to the hype. The burgers are delicious and well prepared and the ability to build your own is nice for those picky eaters who always have to substitute. I got the sricha burger which was very good, but not particularly spicy. The Mac and cheese balls come as a set of 5 and are a great appetizer. Unfortunately the burgers don't come with fries, but you can add them (I chose sweet potato fries). Good selection of beer on tap and there's a full bar if you want something stronger. Finished off the meal with the giant brownie which I do not recommend unless you have four people to share it - it's massive and rich.

Only thing I saw was that there are very few "healthy" options built in. The focus is obviously on the 50/50 beef/bacon burger and not on chicken or turkey. You CAN substitute these in though for what it's worth.  Just disappointed that they don't have a burger built around the chicken.<//Text>

< Time>
1562272498401< /Time>
<rate>4< /rate><review>Great place to have an Impossible Burger which is way superior to Beyond Burgers. Beyond burgers are okay but you can taste and smell the bean protein they have in it. Impossible burgers when cooked right are deliciously crispy on the outside and juicy on the inside. You can't get over how much this plant based patty tastes like actual meat. Umami Burger and Park Bench Cafe also offer Impossible Burgers, but Park Bench overcooks their patty to look and taste like a disgusting McDonald's patty and it was just okay at Umami Burger. Slater's 50/50 makes one hell of an Impossible Burger and its accompaniments were spot on to make a very tasty plant based burger. Glad they make an incredible Impossible burger here in my own backyard that rivals the amazing one I had up in Solvang.

I love taking my dog with me when I go out so the outdoor dog friendly seating was an extra plus. They have a dog menu with items like turkey patty, beef patty, their 50/50 patty and chicken tenders. I brought a bowl for my pup along with some kibbles to mix in with the patty after I cut it up for her.

Negatives were not offering water for my dog when they're a dog friendly establishment and their outdoor seating area was covered in dirt and debris. I had water for my dog, but I find it standard for establishments to offer water in take out containers for your pups nowadays and no offer was made. Even after doing their best to wipe down the tables I had to pull out my own Wet Ones to clean my area more. Other outdoor patios have way better upkeep.

We were all happy with our food and the service was pleasant and quick. Their price is what it is so I'm not going to get angry about it and have it affect my rating, but it will affect how often I come here. I took off one star for the upkeep of their outdoor seating area and not providing that extra above and beyond step offering my dog water to leave a stand out impression on me. I do believe prices were lower when they were at their other location on Adam's. Great if they adjust their prices in the future. If not, then there are plenty of other delicious and diverse food offerings in Southern California at a better price point if you dine out casually frequently. We're busy people and dine out 80% of the week allowing for one guilt free day of eating unhealthy foods. This isn't fine dining by any means, so it does have to bother most sensible people a bit when a burger at a very casual place does seem a bit overpriced. I believe my Impossible Burger was around $18 for anyone that is curious (included a small side of fries with bacon ketchup). On the other hand I went to a fine dining establishment in Solvang and believe I paid a little less for their Impossible burger there, so that is the basis for my comparison.< /review><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< response>
None<//response>

<text>I have eaten here several times and have yet to be disappointed by anything I have tried.  Be prepared to wait a bit if you get there during the lunch rush or dinner rush.  But the wait is well worth it.  The appetizers are great.  I love the fried pickles and especially the vampire dip (I always get it on my burger too).  The burgers are made to order and you can customize them however you want, from different types of meats, buns, condiments, and toppings.  I have not made a burger I haven't loved.  For those in a rush or those that don't want to endlessly customize they have a menu of popular burger choices.  I haven't tried any of them yet but they always look quite tasty.  Their beer selection is great, ranging from your regular beers all the way to several craft beers.  The restaurant is big and a bit noisy but it's a great place for a large group of people or just a fun messy date night.  Go to Slaters if you want a great burger and super filling meal!<//text>< Pics>

<user_id>100075126053886401339</user_id>< Name>
Juliet Salinas</Name>
<date>1539470665099< /date>< Rate>
1<//Rate>
< Text>
My own personal kitchen nightmare:
My wife and I showed up and were seated at a high top.  We got a menu and had to wait around a bit for the server to take our order.  Nothing too crazy, but the place wasn't very busy, so no reason it should have taken that long  (server seemed too busy chatting with his friends or flirting with the girls a few tables down).

We ordered chips and cheese dip with guacamole and two of their 50/50 Original burgers. We waited at least 30-40 minutes and my wife was 5 minutes from walking out when all of our food arrived at once.  Once we'd sampled some of it, we were wishing we'd just left.

The "green chili queso" was clearly just nacho cheese from a can. The guac was a brownish green and watery (Frozen? From a bag?).  The salsa would have been better from a jar...it tasted fairly fresh, but underseasoned, bland.  Like someone just blitzed salsa ingredients in a blender and failed to salt or allow flavors to mingle.

Then the burger.  I'd been looking forward to trying their signature 50/50 beef/bacon patty. Unfortunately it was a huge letdown.  I got a very odd smokiness from it.  Not like wood smoke, but more like a spent firework.  I can only guess it's the nitrates?  The entire burger felt a bit too chewy.  My guess is that they make these way way ahead of time and probably freeze them.  The entire burger felt like it was "cured", rather than being a fresh grind of bacon and beef.

The server comped us the chips and cheese based on the late arrival, but when we asked for our check having only eaten a total of 3 bites of the burgers, and declined to box anything up, he didn't feel it was pertinent to ask if there was anything wrong with our meals.

We paid $33 for a really awful meal and some seriously shoddy service.  I'm giving this place one more star than it deserves.<//Text>

I called in to the hostess and asking if they had any deals or any happy hour she didn't know she didn't know the menu she didn't know the happy hour for the even had one I got there it was not happy hour even though she said there was even though they honored it I got to the happy hour menu the dishes are still relatively expensive but for appetizers they were a lot smaller in size. I ordered one of everything on that appetizer menu I got mozzarella sticks that didn't have cheese in them no mozzarella in them whatsoever I got a bucket of tater tots and there may be about like 15 in there the lettuce wraps or Bland they had no sauce for them whatsoever. The only appetizer I thought that was good was probably the chips and dip the bartender was great her name is blue she was attentive and fulfilling my soda and she was knowledgeable about the beers. The hot dog appetizer pretty much look like one hot dog slicing the three and they charge $6 for it the bread was not bake or heat it up at all so it was cold and kind of stale tasting. The pretzels were overly salted tasted like they were microwaved. I have been here before and I usually get a burger the burgers don't come with sides but the burgers are delicious but they do cost an arm and a leg as well. It's a decent place to watch sports games they have tons of TVs that's why I didn't give it a one. If a friend ever want to try this place I wouldn't necessarily deter them but I would probably eat beforehand because if you're hungry I hope you bring a ton of cash I would still enjoy a game there though< /review>

Ramon Yan<//name>

105922283318214063748</user_id>
< user_name>
Stephanie Han< /user_name>
<Date>1426180792841</Date><rating>5< /rating>< review>
I don't get down to these neck of the woods very often anymore so I hadn't been to this particular Slater's since their grand opening like 2-3 years ago? A few friends and I had a bunch of coupons that we'd won at various events so we decided to get together for their Wed free pub quiz night and make the coupons rain! The six of us got there around 8pm and the place was pretty busy--we had to wait a few minutes to get seated. I've been a fan since they first opened; not just of their food, which has always been good, but of their uniformly congenial, helpful staff. I don't think I've ever run into a rude server at any of their locations and this location was no different, I'm happy to say. From the hostess to our fantastic server Bryan and all the other various servers who assisted him that night, everyone was unfailingly cheerful and helpful, which is no mean feat when it's at the end of a long day and a table wants to slap you with 5 coupons and is constantly asking you for beer samples, lol. Bryan didn't bat an eye to any of it and treated us great all night. That's not to say there weren't a couple of hiccups: a veggie burger came out with a turkey patty and our apps came out at uneven times, but I think those are pretty minor quibbles, all things considered.

I got my usual 50/50 burger, and it was just as good as I remembered--there's something magical about the combination of the avocado mash, their 50/50 patty, the brioche bun and the fried egg. I've tried a bunch of their other burgers but this is the one I always come back to. We got an order of half reg fries and half sweet potato fries, which were also great. The pub quiz was fun, although it was a little hard to hear the announcer guy at times (we were kind of on the outer edge). It's free to play and you win various Slaters-related merch and food (more coupons!). Alas, we didn't come close to placing in the top three but we had a blast, nonetheless. They had happy hour prices during the quiz so that helped, and I didn't even mention the free corkage! We'd brought a couple of bottles of wine with us and we didn't get charged for using their glasses, lol. A nice combination of great customer service and tasty food on this visit!< /review>
< pics>
None</pics>
<Resp>None</Resp><gmapID>0x80dd21311cd07929:0xf8813ae98dd549d7< /gmapID></record>
</dataset><record>
<user>101233080962096726960< /user>< name>
Jason Nordgren< /name>
< date>
1447746021345</date>
<rate>5<//rate>< review>
Wonderful (and wonderfully unhealthy) top shelf burgers. The grilled brussels sprouts are an unexpected but tasty appetizer. Perfectly caramelized and peppered with sinfully delicious thick cut bacon and shaved parmesan. My wife had the (slightly) healthier turkey burger. It was juicy and had a fantastic flavorful punch of rosemary, for her this is now the bar that all other turkey burgers must meet. I had the sriracha burger which was packed with spicy goodness. From the sriracha spiced 50% beef / 50% ground bacon patty, to the need a cigarette afterwards glazed sriracha bacon, to the creamy sriracha aioli, this burger mounts a flavor assault on you taste buds, but stops appropriately short of the scorched earth (tongue) that it could have easily fallen into. We also shared some fried pickles that were a credit to the southern culinary tradition that they came from. The batter was crispy and adhered well to the thick cut house made pickle chips but wasn't too thick and doughy. The servers were very friendly and attentive and as a bonus, the patio outside is dog friendly.</review>
